[2022-11-30, 22:36:08] Deelaka Dias: import time
from tabulate import tabulate
head = ["Name","Age","Team","Car","Points"]

def VCT():
    driver_file = open("Driver_details.txt", 'r')
    read_for_order = driver_file.readlines()
    driver_file.close()
    sorted_file = open("Sorted.txt", 'w')
    list_for_comparing = []
    for line in read_for_order:
        edit_line = line.strip().split(",")
        list_for_comparing.append(edit_line)

    for i in range(len(list_for_comparing)):
        for k in range(i + 1, len(list_for_comparing)):
            if int(list_for_comparing[i][4]) > int(list_for_comparing[k][4]):
                list_for_comparing[i], list_for_comparing[k] = list_for_comparing[k], list_for_comparing[i]

    list_for_comparing.reverse()
    for j in range(1, len(list_for_comparing)):
        sorted_file.write(str(list_for_comparing[j]) + "\n")

    sorted_file.close()
    time.sleep(1.0)
    print("Driver details sorted")

[2023-02-20, 12:05:06] Rushdi IIT: package login;

//importing the libraries

import javafx.application.Application;
import javafx.event.ActionEvent;
import javafx.event.EventHandler;
import javafx.geometry.HPos;
import javafx.geometry.Insets;
import javafx.geometry.Pos;
import javafx.scene.Scene;
import javafx.scene.control.Button;
import javafx.scene.control.Label;
import javafx.scene.control.PasswordField;
import javafx.scene.control.TextField;
import javafx.scene.layout.GridPane;
import javafx.scene.layout.HBox;
import javafx.scene.paint.Color;
import javafx.scene.text.Font;
import javafx.scene.text.FontWeight;
import javafx.scene.text.Text;
import javafx.stage.Stage;


public class Login extends Application {

    public static void main(String[] args) {
        launch(args);
    }

    @Override
    public void start(Stage primaryStage) {
        primaryStage.setTitle("Registation Form JavaFX Application");
        GridPane grid = new GridPane();
        grid.setAlignment(Pos.CENTER);
        grid.setHgap(10);
        grid.setVgap(10);
        grid.setPadding(new Insets(25, 25, 25, 25));

        Text scenetitle = new Text("Registation Form");
        scenetitle.setFont(Font.font("Arial", FontWeight.NORMAL, 20));
        grid.add(scenetitle, 0, 0, 2, 1);
        grid.setHalignment (scenetitle, HPos.CENTER);

        //Full Name Label
        Label fullName = new Label("Full Name:");
        grid.add(fullName, 0, 1);

        //Full Name Field
        TextField userTextField = new TextField();
        grid.add(userTextField, 1, 1);

        //Email ID Label
        Label emailID = new Label("Email ID:");
        grid.add(emailID, 0, 2);

        //Email ID Field
        TextField emailBox = new TextField();
        grid.add(emailBox, 1, 2);

        //Password Label
        Label pw = new Label("Password:");
        grid.add(pw, 0, 3);

        //Password Field
        PasswordField pwBox = new PasswordField();
        grid.add(pwBox, 1, 3);

        Button btn = new Button("Submit");
        HBox hbBtn = new HBox(10);
        hbBtn.setAlignment(Pos.BOTTOM_RIGHT);
        hbBtn.getChildren().add(btn);
        grid.add(hbBtn, 1, 4);

        final Text actiontarget = new Text();
        grid.add(actiontarget, 1, 6);

        btn.setOnAction(new EventHandler<ActionEvent>() {

            @Override
            public void handle(ActionEvent e) {
                actiontarget.setFill(Color.FIREBRICK);
                actiontarget.setText("Submit button pressed");
            }
        });

        Scene scene = new Scene(grid, 600, 300);
        primaryStage.setScene(scene);
        primaryStage.show();
    }
}

//importing form java libraries

import javafx.application.Application;
import javafx.event.ActionEvent;
import javafx.event.EventHandler;
import javafx.geometry.HPos;
import javafx.geometry.Insets;
import javafx.geometry.Pos;
import javafx.scene.Scene;
import javafx.scene.control.Button;
import javafx.scene.control.Label;
import javafx.scene.control.PasswordField;
import javafx.scene.control.TextField;
import javafx.scene.layout.GridPane;
import javafx.scene.layout.HBox;
import javafx.scene.paint.Color;
import javafx.scene.text.Font;
import javafx.scene.text.FontWeight;
import javafx.scene.text.Text;
import javafx.stage.Stage;


public class Login extends Application {

    public static void main(String[] args) {
        launch(args);
    }

    @Override
    public void start(Stage primaryStage) {
        primaryStage.setTitle("Loging in Screen via JavaFx");
        GridPane grid = new GridPane();
        grid.setAlignment(Pos.CENTER);
        grid.setHgap(10);
        grid.setVgap(10);
        grid.setPadding(new Insets(25, 25, 25, 25));

        Text scenetitle = new Text("Registation Form");
        scenetitle.setFont(Font.font("Arial", FontWeight.NORMAL, 20));
        grid.add(scenetitle, 0, 0, 2, 1);
        grid.setHalignment (scenetitle, HPos.CENTER);

        //Full Name Label
        Label fullName = new Label("Full Name:");
        grid.add(fullName, 0, 1);

        //Full Name Field
        TextField userTextField = new TextField();
        grid.add(userTextField, 1, 1);

        //Email ID Label
        Label emailID = new Label("Email Address:");
        grid.add(emailID, 0, 2);

        //Email ID Field
        TextField emailBox = new TextField();
        grid.add(emailBox, 1, 2);

        //Password Label
        Label pw = new Label("Password:");
        grid.add(pw, 0, 3);

        //Password Field
        PasswordField pwBox = new PasswordField();
        grid.add(pwBox, 1, 3);

        Button btn = new Button("-Submit-");
        HBox hbBtn = new HBox(10);
        hbBtn.setAlignment(Pos.BOTTOM_RIGHT);
        hbBtn.getChildren().add(btn);
        grid.add(hbBtn, 1, 4);

        final Text actiontarget = new Text();
        grid.add(actiontarget, 1, 6);

        btn.setOnAction(new EventHandler<ActionEvent>() {

            @Override
            public void handle(ActionEvent e) {
                actiontarget.setFill(Color.FIREBRICK);
                actiontarget.setText("Submit button pressed");
            }
        });

        Scene scene = new Scene(grid, 600, 300);
        primaryStage.setScene(scene);
        primaryStage.show();
    }
}

There are many potential avenues for research on stress management, including the development of new techniques and therapies, the evaluation of existing treatments, and the identification of risk factors and protective factors for stress.
In terms of market potential, the stress management market is expected to grow significantly in the coming years. According to a report by MarketsandMarkets, the global stress management market was valued at $8.5 billion in 2019 and is projected to reach $11.0 billion by 2024, growing at a compound annual growth rate (CAGR) of 5.2%.

Overall, there is significant market potential for stress management research, with a growing demand for effective stress management solutions.

[2023-02-25, 23:57:14] Deelaka Dias: business model for stress management software
A business model for a stress management software might include the following elements:

Value Proposition: The software should address a clear pain point for customers - in this case, stress management. It should offer a unique and valuable solution that meets the needs of users seeking to manage their stress levels.

Revenue Streams: There are a few different options for generating revenue from a stress management software. One common approach is to charge a subscription fee for access to premium features or content. Another option is to offer the software for free and generate revenue through advertising or partnerships with related companies.

Customer Segments: The software should be designed to meet the needs of specific customer segments. For example, it might target individuals who suffer from chronic stress, busy professionals who struggle to balance work and personal life, or students dealing with academic pressure.

Channels: There are a variety of channels that could be used to market the software and reach potential customers. These might include social media ads, content marketing, influencer partnerships, or referral programs.

Key Activities: The key activities for a stress management software might include software development, content creation (e.g. guided meditations, stress management tips), marketing and advertising, and customer support.

Key Resources: The key resources for a stress management software might include a strong team of developers, designers, and content creators, as well as access to relevant industry research and data.

Partnerships: Partnerships can help to increase the reach and effectiveness of the software. For example, partnering with mental health organizations, yoga studios, or fitness apps could help to promote the software and provide additional value to customers.

Cost Structure: The cost structure for a stress management software will depend on a variety of factors, including the cost of software development, content creation, marketing, and customer support. It may also include ongoing costs related to hosting, maintenance, and updates to the software.

[2023-02-26, 00:27:30] Deelaka Dias: Stress management software is designed to help individuals manage and reduce their stress levels. It can be used by individuals or by organizations to promote mental health and productivity in the workplace.

Here are some technical aspects of stress management software:

Features: Stress management software may include features such as guided meditation, breathing exercises, relaxation techniques, cognitive-behavioral therapy (CBT) exercises, goal setting, and progress tracking.

User interface: The software should have an intuitive and user-friendly interface to allow users to navigate and access the features easily.

Compatibility: Stress management software should be compatible with various devices and operating systems such as desktop computers, laptops, tablets, and smartphones. This will enable users to access the software from anywhere at any time.

Security: Stress management software should be designed with security in mind to protect user data and ensure privacy. It should use encryption protocols to secure user data during transmission and storage.

Integration: Stress management software should be able to integrate with other tools and applications such as fitness trackers, wearable devices, and productivity apps to provide a comprehensive wellness solution.

Data analytics: Stress management software should provide analytics and reporting capabilities to help users and organizations monitor progress and identify areas for improvement.

Customization: Stress management software should allow users to customize their experience based on their preferences and needs. This may include setting reminders, selecting preferred meditation music, and adjusting the difficulty level of exercises.

Overall, stress management software can be a valuable tool for individuals and organizations seeking to improve mental health and productivity. The software should be designed with the user in mind, offer a range of features, be secure and customizable, and provide data analytics and reporting capabilities.
[2023-02-26, 00:30:53] Deelaka Dias: social impact on stress management software

Stress management software can have a positive social impact by helping individuals manage their stress levels and improve their overall well-being. Here are a few ways in which stress management software can have a social impact:

Improved Mental Health: Stress management software can help individuals identify the sources of their stress and provide them with tools to manage it effectively. By doing so, it can help reduce symptoms of anxiety and depression, which can have a positive impact on their social life by improving their mood and reducing social isolation.

Increased Productivity: When individuals are stressed, it can impact their productivity and ability to work effectively. By providing tools to manage stress, such as mindfulness exercises and time management techniques, stress management software can help individuals become more productive at work. This can have a positive social impact by helping them achieve their goals and contribute to society.

Better Relationships: Stress can negatively impact relationships with family, friends, and coworkers. By helping individuals manage their stress, stress management software can improve their communication skills, reduce conflicts, and enhance their overall social interactions.

Healthier Lifestyle: Stress management software can encourage individuals to adopt a healthier lifestyle by promoting regular exercise, healthy eating, and good sleep habits. This can have a positive social impact by reducing healthcare costs, improving overall health, and promoting a healthier society.

Overall, stress management software can have a positive social impact by promoting mental health, productivity, better relationships, and a healthier lifestyle.
[2023-02-26, 00:32:18] Deelaka Dias: competitor analysis on stress management software 

A competitor analysis on stress management software would involve researching and evaluating other companies offering similar products in the market. Here are the steps you could take to conduct a competitor analysis on stress management software:

Identify Competitors: Begin by identifying competitors in the market. Use search engines, app stores, and other sources to find companies offering stress management software.

Evaluate Product Offerings: Once you've identified your competitors, evaluate their product offerings. Look at the features and functionalities of their software, their pricing models, and user feedback to understand their strengths and weaknesses.

Analyze Marketing Strategies: Examine the marketing strategies used by your competitors. Look at their website design, content marketing efforts, social media presence, and advertising campaigns. This will help you understand how they are positioning their product in the market.

Assess Customer Base: Analyze your competitors' customer base. Look at the demographics, geographics, and psychographics of their users to understand who they are targeting and how they are reaching them.

Conduct SWOT Analysis: Use a SWOT analysis to evaluate your competitors' strengths, weaknesses, opportunities, and threats. This will help you identify areas where you can differentiate your product from theirs.

Determine Competitive Advantage: Based on the information gathered, determine your competitive advantage. Identify what sets your product apart from your competitors and how you can use this to position your product in the market.

Overall, a competitor analysis on stress management software involves evaluating the competition, understanding their strengths and weaknesses, and using this information to develop a strategy to differentiate your product in the market.

[2023-03-22, 11:51:44] Deelaka Dias: class Queue {
    int front;
    public int rear;
    public int noOfItems;
    private int maxSize;
    public float[] queueArray;
    public int count = 0;

    public void Queue(int size) {
        maxSize = size; // length of the queue Array
        front = 0; // most first element in the queue
        rear = -1;
        noOfItems = 0; // number of elements in the queue Array
        queueArray = new float[maxSize]; // creating new queue array
    }

    //isFull and isEmpty methods
    public boolean isFull() {
        return (rear + 1 == maxSize); // checking if queue array is full
    }

    public boolean isEmpty() {
        return (noOfItems == 0); // checking if queue array is empty
    }

    //Enqueue method
    public void enqueue(float item) {
        if (isFull()) {
            System.out.println("You have entered the total number of transactions you ");
        } else {
            queueArray[++rear] = item;
            noOfItems++;
        }
    }

    //Dequeue method
    public float dequeue() {
        if (isEmpty()) {
            System.out.println("You have successfully sold all stocks\n");
            return 0;
        } else {
            noOfItems--;
            return queueArray[front++];
        }
    }

    public float peek() {
        if (isEmpty()) {
            System.out.println("You have successfully sold all stocks\n");
            return 0;
        }
        return queueArray[front];
    }


    // if there are any remaining share after the sell, of the specified shares slot, then replace them to the front element.
    public void replace(float n) {  // parsing remaining shares to this parameter called n
        --front;
        queueArray[front] = n;
        ++noOfItems;
        count++;
    }
}
